< Review>
This is a unique experience. The drive out to the destination is quite an adventure by itself. Definitely recommend 4 wheel drive or at least a hearty SUV with traction control. Once at the trailhead, the initial hike to the caves is quite strenuous, but short. The caves are a lot of fun to explore. There are some very large ones that can fit multiple people, there are some that go through to the other side. Amazing views from the top too.< /Review>

<Resp>None</Resp>< text>
Very suggestive place, I wouldn't come here in the middle of summer, unless you really like the heat. We were here in November, and it was just bearable! We really liked it. You need to have a 4X car or you can't drive here. We left our car a little forward the end of the paved street. During the weekend there's a lot of locals that go and drive their 4x down this way, so if you're lucky (like we were) you can get a lift here and back, otherwise I would say it's about 2hours hike each way. Most of it in the sun. If you do so, bring with you PLENTY of water, more is always better than not enough!</text>

If you walk instead of drive to the wind caves, it you'll be putting in about 10 miles of hiking total. Bring enough water if you plan to walk the whole thing!! Obviously, it's much faster if you drive but you don't get to marvel in all the geological beauty that is split mountain. It's worth the walk, at least once. The Arby's, Del Taco, Pet hospital, donut shop and haircut shop are all the same as 30 years ago. The parking lot is generally clean except near the 99 cent store as people throw their garbage everywhere.  Be careful parking near the 99 cent store as people will cart your vehicle because they don't know what a return corral is. Best bet is to park a bit away from the store front.</Text>
